          "text": "Cloned from launchpad blueprint https://blueprints.launchpad.net/sahara/+spec/edp-refactor-job-manager.\n\nDescription:\n\nThe original job manager was written to execute and monitor jobs via an Oozie server.  As we add new provisioning plugin types, for example the Spark plugin, we will need new EDP implementations for clusters that do not support Oozie.\n\nThere are 3 basic operations that the job manager currently performs:\n* run a job\n* get job status\n* cancel a job\n\nIf the job manager can select a class which implements these three operations for a particular cluster, then the job manager can be generalized and deal only with high level logic and update of job execution objects.\n\n(detailed spec on its way)\n\nSpecification URL (additional information):\n\nNone",

      "summary": "[RFE][cinder]: Make handling of ssh host keys configurable for Cinder", 
      "external_bugs": [], 
      "id": "1110592", 
      "cf_release_notes": "", 
      "priority": "unspecified", 
      "severity": "unspecified", 
      "is_confirmed": "True", 
      "is_creator_accessible": "True", 
      "cf_fixed_in": "", 
      "creator": "rhos-integ@redhat.com", 
      "comments": [
        {
          "count": "0", 
          "creator": "rhos-integ@redhat.com", 
          "text": "Cloned from launchpad blueprint https://blueprints.launchpad.net/cinder/+spec/configurable-ssh-host-key-policy.\n\nDescription:\n\nTo address concerns of weak SSH security in Cinder, the way that\nssh host keys are handled by Cinder should be configurable, allowing\nsystem administrators to choose how secure they wish their SSH connections\nto be.\n\nThis blueprint proposes making the way that SSH\nhost keys are handled configurable, allowing system administrators\nto make a conscious decision about the level of security they need\non their system.\n\nThe solution would require two new configuration items as well as\na change to the current default behavior.  First, there would need\nto a 'strict_ssh_host_key_policy' configuration option with possible\nsettings of 'false' (default) or 'true'.  When this option is set to\n'false' it will automatically accept the host key on the first connection\nand then will throw an exception if the host key changes in the future.\nThis is where the default behavior changes from the current functionality.\n\nIn the case that 'strict_ssh_host_key_policy' is set to 'true' then a\nsecond option 'ssh_host_keys_file' must be configured.  When the strict\nconfiguration is used it is assumed that the administrator is going to\nhave pre-configured ssh host keys and any deviation from those expected\nkeys will be handled with an exception.\n\nSpecification URL (additional information):\n\nNone", 
          "author": "rhos-integ@redhat.com", 
          "creation_time": "20140618T04:08:01", 
          "bug_id": "1110592", 
          "creator_id": "360918", 
          "time": "20140618T04:08:01", 
          "id": "7207217", 
          "is_private": "False"
        }
      ],

      "summary": "[RFE][cinder]: Pool-aware Scheduler Support", 
      "external_bugs": [], 
      "id": "1110595", 
      "cf_release_notes": "", 
      "priority": "unspecified", 
      "severity": "unspecified", 
      "is_confirmed": "True", 
      "is_creator_accessible": "True", 
      "cf_fixed_in": "", 
      "creator": "rhos-integ@redhat.com", 
      "comments": [
        {
          "count": "0", 
          "creator": "rhos-integ@redhat.com", 
          "text": "Cloned from launchpad blueprint https://blueprints.launchpad.net/cinder/+spec/pool-aware-cinder-scheduler.\n\nDescription:\n\nCinder has been designed to take look each volume backend as a whole since day 1.  The provisioning decisions are based on the statistics reported by backends periodically.  Any back end is assumed to be a single discrete unit with specific set of capabilities and capacities offered and also these characteristics are constant through out the boundary of the storage addressed/managed by the back end.   In reality this assumption is not true for many storage providers and as their storage managed can be further sub divided or partitioned into 'pools' to offer completely different set of capabilities and capacities.  That is there are storage backends are a combination of storage pools rather than one big single homogenous entity.  And usually volumes/snapshots can't be placed across pools on such backends.   As a result, there are several obvious problems when using them with current Cinder:\n1.  A volume/snapshot that is larger than any sub-pool of the target backend be schedule the backend would fail;\n2.  A sub pool may not have enough space to serve consecutive request (e.g. clone volume, create snapshot) but while the entire backend appears to have enough capacity;\nThe issues are very confusing and result in inconsistent user experience.  Therefore it is important to extend cinder to be aware of storage pools within backend and also use them as finest granularity for resource placement.   \n\nSpecification URL (additional information):\n\nNone", 
          "author": "rhos-integ@redhat.com",

        {
          "count": "0", 
          "creator": "jzeleny@redhat.com", 
          "text": "+++ This bug was initially created as a clone of Bug #1099394 +++\n\nDescription of problem:\nA simple and minimally invasive way to improve support for SCLs exported over NFS would be to allow an \"scl import\" command, or something similar, which sets up /etc/scl for a collection which is not packaged natively.\n\nMaybe \"scl register\" would make more sense for naming the action?\n\nVersion-Release number of selected component (if applicable):\nscl-utils-20120927-8.el6.1.x86_64\n\nExample of required behaviour:\n# mount server:/opt/rh /opt/rh\n# scl import /opt/rh/php54 /opt/rh/perl516\n# cat /etc/scl/prefixes/php54\n/opt/rh\n# cat /etc/scl/prefixes/perl516\n/opt/rh\n\n--- Additional comment from V\u00edt Ondruch on 2014-05-20 14:53:24 CEST ---\n\n/etc/scl/prefixes/* does not make sense. Why it should go to /etc? It should go into var and treated carefully, since the mount may disappear virtually any moment.\n\nMoreover, from that point of view, anything such as \"scl import\" does not make sense. Why you need to import it? User probably knows that (s)he wants to run \"scl enable ruby193\". If that fails, the message should provide reasonable explanation. The only interesting command is \"scl list\" which lists available collections and I can't see any reason, why this command should not go through /opt and look form some familiar directory structure or file.\n\n--- Additional comment from Jan Zeleny on 2014-05-20 17:43:16 CEST ---\n\n(In reply to V\u00edt Ondruch from comment #1)\n> /etc/scl/prefixes/* does not make sense. Why it should go to /etc? It should\n> go into var and treated carefully, since the mount may disappear virtually\n> any moment.\n\nI'm pretty sure we have an RFE with this request targeted at Fedora and upstream. Nothing like that is going to be done in RHEL6 for obvious reasons.\n\n> Moreover, from that point of view, anything such as \"scl import\" does not\n> make sense. Why you need to import it? User probably knows that (s)he wants\n> to run \"scl enable ruby193\". If that fails, the message should provide\n> reasonable explanation. The only interesting command is \"scl list\" which\n> lists available collections and I can't see any reason, why this command\n> should not go through /opt and look form some familiar directory structure\n> or file.\n\nManually importing is the only possible way in situation where scl-utils can't know for sure where is the collection root (in this context, /opt is just the best practice but you don't want to base a supported solution on the assumption that everyone will follow the best practice) and what is its layout (again, each collection can be built with a completely different build configuration).\n\nNote that this enhancement is actually something like official workaround to compensate for design gaps of scl-utils.\n\n--- Additional comment from V\u00edt Ondruch on 2014-05-21 10:23:39 CEST ---\n\nWouldn't be better to allow something like \"scl enable rh/ruby193\" as a official workaround? I.e. only the /opt would be assumed and the rest would be full path to the collection main directory/enable scriptlet.\n\nDoing some links or pseudo installation, which would allow to \"scl list\" work, but also to report wrong information does not make sense to me.\n\n--- Additional comment from Jan Zeleny on 2014-05-22 08:32:33 CEST ---\n\n(In reply to V\u00edt Ondruch from comment #3)\n> Wouldn't be better to allow something like \"scl enable rh/ruby193\" as a\n> official workaround? I.e. only the /opt would be assumed and the rest would\n> be full path to the collection main directory/enable scriptlet.\n\nActually the only part that can be safely taken for granted in the current design is that there is a root/ directory somewhere and that there are some bash scripts on the same level of the filesystem hierarchy. Every other piece of the path is just pure assumption, as it can be tweaked ate build time. Note that there can even be more levels of hierarchy (/opt/rh/jzeleny/colXYZ) or there might be multiple collection mounts on the system (take a look at the FPC proposal in Fedora where they wanted to have two different locations for collections).\n\n> Doing some links or pseudo installation, which would allow to \"scl list\"\n> work, but also to report wrong information does not make sense to me.\n\nIt's all about user expectations. When user expects that NFS mounts have to be \"imported\" first for the listing functionality to work, then we should be ok.\n\n--- Additional comment from V\u00edt Ondruch on 2014-05-22 08:57:22 CEST ---\n\n(In reply to Jan Zeleny from comment #4)\n> (In reply to V\u00edt Ondruch from comment #3)\n> > Wouldn't be better to allow something like \"scl enable rh/ruby193\" as a\n> > official workaround? I.e. only the /opt would be assumed and the rest would\n> > be full path to the collection main directory/enable scriptlet.\n> \n> Actually the only part that can be safely taken for granted in the current\n> design is that there is a root/ directory somewhere and that there are some\n> bash scripts on the same level of the filesystem hierarchy. Every other\n> piece of the path is just pure assumption, as it can be tweaked ate build\n> time. Note that there can even be more levels of hierarchy\n> (/opt/rh/jzeleny/colXYZ) or there might be multiple collection mounts on the\n> system (take a look at the FPC proposal in Fedora where they wanted to have\n> two different locations for collections).\n\nAccepting full path to collection root is Ok with me. Or as an alternative, I can imagine to specify something like SCL_PATHS env variable, where the roots will be specified and just the short name will enough to enable the collection.\n\n> > Doing some links or pseudo installation, which would allow to \"scl list\"\n> > work, but also to report wrong information does not make sense to me.\n> \n> It's all about user expectations. When user expects that NFS mounts have to\n> be \"imported\" first for the listing functionality to work, then we should be\n> ok.\n\nIt is OK just at the time of import. Later, the \"import\" may cause, that \"scl list\" will return some list of collection, but you could not trust it anyway. In that case, I am very much in favor of getting list of available collections by \"ls /opt/rh\" or whatever the location might be and forget about importing.\n\n--- Additional comment from Jan Zeleny on 2014-05-22 15:37:32 CEST ---\n\nI hear your concern about collection list getting inaccurate over time, thank you for your feedback. I still stand by Joe's original design though.\n\nThat being said, if product management explicitly and fully supports the assessment in your last comment and you provide the patch, I will happily include it.",

(List the business requirements here)  \n  \nGSS has encountered a number of instances where customers are unaware of the limitations of local storage, and run into issues with production VMs where there is no resolution without downtime because the VMs are running on local storage\n\n How would the customer like to achieve this? (List the functional requirements here)  \n\nFirst - alerts tot he user during initial configuration of local storage DCs/hypervisors.       "summary": "[RFE][ironic]: Discover node properties automatically at node-create and node-update", 
      "external_bugs": [], 
      "id": "1110992", 
      "cf_release_notes": "", 
      "priority": "unspecified", 
      "severity": "unspecified", 
      "is_confirmed": "True", 
      "is_creator_accessible": "True", 
      "cf_fixed_in": "", 
      "creator": "rhos-integ@redhat.com", 
      "comments": [
        {
          "count": "0", 
          "creator": "rhos-integ@redhat.com", 
          "text": "Cloned from launchpad blueprint https://blueprints.launchpad.net/ironic/+spec/ironic-node-properties-discovery.\n\nDescription:\n\nIronic does not have the out-of-band node properties discovery.\nThe proposal is to discover node properties automatically\nirrespective of whether OS is deployed on the baremetal node or not.\n\nSome of the properties which are of interest are listed below:\n\n* memory size\n\n* memory addressing (64 bit/32 bit)\n\n* Disk Size\n\n* CPUs\n\n* CPU architecture\n\n* Supported Boot Modes\n\n* Current Boot Mode\n\n* BIOS/UEFI Firmware Version\n\n* Number of NICs\n\n* NIC(s) MAC address\n\nA driver can discover more properties than listed above.\n\nThis proposal adds the ability to perform out-of-band\nnode property discovery and automatically update\nnode properties during ironic node-create process\nwhen driver_info fields are provided in the command line\nlike BMC ip address, access credentials etc.\n\nironic node-create -d ilo -i <ilo_address=value> ... -i <iLOClient_timeout=value>\n\nThe node-update can be modified to have a new option, say\n'--discover' which can be invoked when any hardware changes happen.\nThis will update the node property info automatically again.\n\n# ironic node-update <node_uuid> --discover <true/false/True/False>\n\nSimilarly, the node-create and node-update can be updated to\nhave a new option, say --create_ports to automatically create\nports with the NIC MAC addresses returned by node-create.\nThe create_ports option will create ports only when the node\nproperties are discovered automatically or with --discover\noption as proposed. The --create_ports option shall not be\nused without --discover option in the node-update.\n\nThe --create_ports option creates port for all the MAC addresses\ndiscovered. If a port already exists for a MAC address, it\nwill not create a new port for that MAC address. The created\nport-ids can be added in the properties info field of the\nnode. This will help user to identify which ports are auto-created\nwith node-create or node-update.\n\n# ironic node-create -d ilo -i <ilo_address=value> ... <iLOClient_timeout=value>\n\n# ironic node-create -d ilo -i <ilo_address=value> ... <iLOClient_timeout=value> --create_ports\n\n# ironic node-update <node_uuid> --discover <true/false/True/False>\n\n# ironic node-update <node_uuid> --discover <true/false/True/False> --create_ports <true/false/True/False>\n\nA new method discover_hardware_properties() will be added\nunder base.ManagementInterface(). This method can be implemented by\ndriver to fetch hardware properties from the baremetal node.\n\nThe iLO driver will implement the above proposal and the method\ndiscover_hardware_properties() which will be used\nto fetch the hardware properties from the Baremetal Node.\nThe iLO driver will use the iLO python library module in proliantUtils\nlibrary to get hardware properties.\n(https://github.com/hpproliant/proliantutils)\n\nSpecification URL (additional information):\n\nNone",

Feature Name:  Short, descriptive, unique name\n  Enable qemu-kvm Inter VM Shared Memory (IVSHM) feature\n\n2. More Detailed Description \n a. Architectures:  x86_64\n b. Dependencies:\n c. External links:\n d. Priority (H,M,L):  High\n e. Proposed Target Releases:  RHEL7.1\n f. Target Release Date:\n g. Drivers or hardware dependency:   Feature is hardware independent\n h. Target Linux Kernel\n i. Any documentation available or required\n\n3. Business Justification info needed:\n a. Why is this feature needed?  \n    This feature enables communication using shared memory between guest\n    and user level program running on host machine, and can achieve\n    10 times performance gain compared to existing virtio interface.\n b. What hardware does this enable?\n    NEC plans to use this feature to implement NFV function on RHEL OSP\n    for carrier grade usage.\n\n c. Is the requester doing the engineering necessary?.\n c. Are you requesting that *Red Hat* do coding and/or upstream work? \n d. Requestor commitment to test?\n\n5. Hardware Provided to RH?\n\n--- Additional comment from Kosuke TATSUKAWA on 2014-06-03 04:04:55 EDT ---\n\nWe heard from Red Hat KK that that another partner has requested this\nfeature as bug 787463, but that parnter has withdrawn the reqeust.\n\nNEC would like to know why this feature was removed from RHEL7.0\n\n--- Additional comment from RHEL Product and Program Management on 2014-06-03 04:19:23 EDT ---\n\nSince this bug report was entered in bugzilla, the release flag has been\nset to ? to ensure that it is properly evaluated for this release.\n\n--- Additional comment from Andrew Jones on 2014-06-04 05:34:45 EDT ---\n\n(In reply to Kosuke TATSUKAWA from comment #1)\n> We heard from Red Hat KK that that another partner has requested this\n> feature as bug 787463, but that parnter has withdrawn the reqeust.\n> \n> NEC would like to know why this feature was removed from RHEL7.0\n\n\nHello Kosuke,\n\nThe consensus has been that while ivshmem could be a useful developer tool, it isn't generally the ''right way'' to go when developing a product. The last partner that requested ivshmem acknowledged that, and in the end switched to using a virtio interface. Here is an incomplete list of reasons ivshmem should probably be a last resort for products\n\n1. It's difficult to maintain products built on ivshmem\n   a. allows custom (read difficult to maintain/port) interfaces to be used\n   b. no upstream kernel uio driver exists - requiring a custom driver to be maintained by each user\n   c. no upstream ivshmem eventfd server exists - requiring a custom server to be maintained by each user\n\n2. Using ivshmem binds guests to particular hosts - i.e. kills live migration\n\n\n\nAdditionally, as it hasn't yet been selected for products, and hasn't yet been supported\n\n3. Using ivshmem could potentially open security holes - no auditing has been conducted yet\n\n4. ivshmem hasn't been well maintained upstream, e.g. it still has poor error handling\n\n5. no libvirt support exists\n\nThe additional points 3-5, and even 1b and 1c, can be addressed, but they'll take time (7.1 is too optimistic, IMHO). There is no solution for 1a, and it'd be very unlikely that we'd want to try to solve 2.\n\nI'd prefer that NEC give us the requirements that ivshmem is currently solving. If we may know exactly how NEC is using ivshmem, and what performance is required, then we may be able to suggest alternative approaches, and possibly improve those alternatives to meet the requirements.\n\nThanks,\ndrew",

          "text": "+++ This bug was initially created as a clone of Bug #1099394 +++\n\nDescription of problem:\nA simple and minimally invasive way to improve support for SCLs exported over NFS would be to allow an \"scl import\" command, or something similar, which sets up /etc/scl for a collection which is not packaged natively.\n\nMaybe \"scl register\" would make more sense for naming the action?\n\nVersion-Release number of selected component (if applicable):\nscl-utils-20120927-8.el6.1.x86_64\n\nExample of required behaviour:\n# mount server:/opt/rh /opt/rh\n# scl import /opt/rh/php54 /opt/rh/perl516\n# cat /etc/scl/prefixes/php54\n/opt/rh\n# cat /etc/scl/prefixes/perl516\n/opt/rh\n\n--- Additional comment from V\u00edt Ondruch on 2014-05-20 08:53:24 EDT ---\n\n/etc/scl/prefixes/* does not make sense. Why it should go to /etc? It should go into var and treated carefully, since the mount may disappear virtually any moment.\n\nMoreover, from that point of view, anything such as \"scl import\" does not make sense. Why you need to import it? User probably knows that (s)he wants to run \"scl enable ruby193\". If that fails, the message should provide reasonable explanation. The only interesting command is \"scl list\" which lists available collections and I can't see any reason, why this command should not go through /opt and look form some familiar directory structure or file.\n\n--- Additional comment from Jan Zeleny on 2014-05-20 11:43:16 EDT ---\n\n(In reply to V\u00edt Ondruch from comment #1)\n> /etc/scl/prefixes/* does not make sense. Why it should go to /etc? It should\n> go into var and treated carefully, since the mount may disappear virtually\n> any moment.\n\nI'm pretty sure we have an RFE with this request targeted at Fedora and upstream. Nothing like that is going to be done in RHEL6 for obvious reasons.\n\n> Moreover, from that point of view, anything such as \"scl import\" does not\n> make sense. Why you need to import it? User probably knows that (s)he wants\n> to run \"scl enable ruby193\". If that fails, the message should provide\n> reasonable explanation. The only interesting command is \"scl list\" which\n> lists available collections and I can't see any reason, why this command\n> should not go through /opt and look form some familiar directory structure\n> or file.\n\nManually importing is the only possible way in situation where scl-utils can't know for sure where is the collection root (in this context, /opt is just the best practice but you don't want to base a supported solution on the assumption that everyone will follow the best practice) and what is its layout (again, each collection can be built with a completely different build configuration).\n\nNote that this enhancement is actually something like official workaround to compensate for design gaps of scl-utils.\n\n--- Additional comment from V\u00edt Ondruch on 2014-05-21 04:23:39 EDT ---\n\nWouldn't be better to allow something like \"scl enable rh/ruby193\" as a official workaround? I.e. only the /opt would be assumed and the rest would be full path to the collection main directory/enable scriptlet.\n\nDoing some links or pseudo installation, which would allow to \"scl list\" work, but also to report wrong information does not make sense to me.\n\n--- Additional comment from Jan Zeleny on 2014-05-22 02:32:33 EDT ---\n\n(In reply to V\u00edt Ondruch from comment #3)\n> Wouldn't be better to allow something like \"scl enable rh/ruby193\" as a\n> official workaround? I.e. only the /opt would be assumed and the rest would\n> be full path to the collection main directory/enable scriptlet.\n\nActually the only part that can be safely taken for granted in the current design is that there is a root/ directory somewhere and that there are some bash scripts on the same level of the filesystem hierarchy. Every other piece of the path is just pure assumption, as it can be tweaked ate build time. Note that there can even be more levels of hierarchy (/opt/rh/jzeleny/colXYZ) or there might be multiple collection mounts on the system (take a look at the FPC proposal in Fedora where they wanted to have two different locations for collections).\n\n> Doing some links or pseudo installation, which would allow to \"scl list\"\n> work, but also to report wrong information does not make sense to me.\n\nIt's all about user expectations. When user expects that NFS mounts have to be \"imported\" first for the listing functionality to work, then we should be ok.\n\n--- Additional comment from V\u00edt Ondruch on 2014-05-22 02:57:22 EDT ---\n\n(In reply to Jan Zeleny from comment #4)\n> (In reply to V\u00edt Ondruch from comment #3)\n> > Wouldn't be better to allow something like \"scl enable rh/ruby193\" as a\n> > official workaround? I.e. only the /opt would be assumed and the rest would\n> > be full path to the collection main directory/enable scriptlet.\n> \n> Actually the only part that can be safely taken for granted in the current\n> design is that there is a root/ directory somewhere and that there are some\n> bash scripts on the same level of the filesystem hierarchy. Every other\n> piece of the path is just pure assumption, as it can be tweaked ate build\n> time. Note that there can even be more levels of hierarchy\n> (/opt/rh/jzeleny/colXYZ) or there might be multiple collection mounts on the\n> system (take a look at the FPC proposal in Fedora where they wanted to have\n> two different locations for collections).\n\nAccepting full path to collection root is Ok with me. Or as an alternative, I can imagine to specify something like SCL_PATHS env variable, where the roots will be specified and just the short name will enough to enable the collection.\n\n> > Doing some links or pseudo installation, which would allow to \"scl list\"\n> > work, but also to report wrong information does not make sense to me.\n> \n> It's all about user expectations. When user expects that NFS mounts have to\n> be \"imported\" first for the listing functionality to work, then we should be\n> ok.\n\nIt is OK just at the time of import. Later, the \"import\" may cause, that \"scl list\" will return some list of collection, but you could not trust it anyway. In that case, I am very much in favor of getting list of available collections by \"ls /opt/rh\" or whatever the location might be and forget about importing.\n\n--- Additional comment from Jan Zeleny on 2014-05-22 09:37:32 EDT ---\n\nI hear your concern about collection list getting inaccurate over time, thank you for your feedback. I still stand by Joe's original design though.\n\nThat being said, if product management explicitly and fully supports the assessment in your last comment and you provide the patch, I will happily include it.",

          "text": "+++ This bug is a RHEV-M zstream clone. The original bug is: +++\n+++   https://bugzilla.redhat.com/show_bug.cgi?id=1078206. +++\n+++ Requested by ''sbonazzo@redhat.com'' +++\n======================================================================\n\n\n\n----------------------------------------------------------------------\nFollowing comment by ederevea@redhat.com on March 19 at 11:48:23, 2014\n\nDescription of problem:\nDuring hosted engine setup, the list of interfaces is provided to use as base for the ''rhevm'' network. However, if a bond is selected, the setup fails.\n\nVersion-Release number of selected component (if applicable):\n3.3.1\n\nHow reproducible:\nalways\n\nSteps to Reproduce:\n1. set up RHEL server, set up bond0 and rhevm33 repos\n2. try to install hosted engine with rhev-m on bond0 (''hosted-engine --deploy'')\n\nActual results:\nSetup finishes with error:\n\n[ INFO  ] Configuring the management bridge\n[ ERROR ] Failed to execute stage 'Misc configuration': 'bond0'\n\n\nExpected results:\nSetup finishes successfully\n\n----------------------------------------------------------------------\nFollowing comment by ederevea@redhat.com on March 19 at 12:00:49, 2014\n\nHere is an explanation and fix proposed by customer:\n\nThe script /usr/share/ovirt-hosted-engine-setup/plugins/ovirt-hosted-engine-setup/network/bridge.py contains a bug. While the representation of the information in the VDSM has changed, in the bridge.py it was not taken into account.\n\nThe script currently searches for the network interface in this way:\n\n    def _misc(self):\n        self.logger.info(_('Configuring the management bridge'))\n        nics = self.environment[ohostedcons.NetworkEnv.BRIDGE_IF]\n        iface = nics\n        caps = self.environment[\n            ohostedcons.VDSMEnv.VDS_CLI\n        ].s.getVdsCapabilities()['info']['nics'][nics]\n        self.logger.debug(\n            'getVdsCaps for {iface}: {caps}'.format(\n                iface=iface,\n                caps=caps,\n            )\n        )\n        bond = ''\n        if netinfo.isbonding(nics):\n            bond = nics\n            nics = ','.join(netinfo.slaves(bond))\n\nI have changed this to the following, just to verify that this is the root cause:\n\n    def _misc(self):\n        self.logger.info(_('Configuring the management bridge'))\n        nics = self.environment[ohostedcons.NetworkEnv.BRIDGE_IF]\n        iface = nics\n        if netinfo.isbonding(nics):\n            caps = self.environment[\n                ohostedcons.VDSMEnv.VDS_CLI\n            ].s.getVdsCapabilities()['info']['bondings'][nics]\n        else:\n            caps = self.environment[\n                ohostedcons.VDSMEnv.VDS_CLI\n            ].s.getVdsCapabilities()['info']['nics'][nics]\n        self.logger.debug(\n            'getVdsCaps for {iface}: {caps}'.format(\n                iface=iface,\n                caps=caps,\n            )\n        )\n        bond = ''\n        if netinfo.isbonding(nics):\n            bond = nics\n            nics = ','.join(netinfo.slaves(bond))\n\nSo if the interface is bonded (netinfo.isbonding(nics)), it is searched for in the proper section (getVdsCapabilities()['info']['bondings'][nics]).\nWith this modification the bridge has been successfully created and the setup passed this point.\n\n----------------------------------------------------------------------\nFollowing comment by sbonazzo@redhat.com on March 19 at 14:18:17, 2014\n\ndidi, above patch looks good, can you apply it and verify it works?\nNote that I just sent a patch adding also vlan support (http://gerrit.ovirt.org/25894) so maybe we need to rebase one of the 2.\n\n----------------------------------------------------------------------\nFollowing comment by sbonazzo@redhat.com on March 19 at 15:48:30, 2014\n\n*** Bug 1076947 has been marked as a duplicate of this bug. ***\n\n----------------------------------------------------------------------\nFollowing comment by sbonazzo@redhat.com on March 20 at 10:37:31, 2014\n\nI'll verify it\n\n----------------------------------------------------------------------\nFollowing comment by sbonazzo@redhat.com on March 20 at 12:56:18, 2014\n\nEvgheni I had to adapt your change with ongoing changes for supporting vlans and it doesn't work for me.           "text": "+++ This bug was initially created as a clone of Bug #823882 +++\n\nRFE Request\n\n0. Proposed title of this feature request\nFeature Request: better memory management in logconv.pl\n\n1. Who is the customer behind the request?\n      Account name: Gerrit Maarten Molenaar (Rabobank Nederland)\n      Customer segment: 1\n      Strategic: Yes\n      TAM/SRM customer yes/no: yes\n      VHT score: 0\n\n2. What is the nature and description of the request?\nFeature Request: better memory management in logconv.pl\n\n3. Why does the customer need this? (List the business requirements here)\nSince with Directory Server Red Hat offer an enterprise solution, a company should be able to expect enterprise behaviour, in this case that is that the product won't break from regular use. This is what's happening with the use of logconv.pl: we use it to handle an undefined amount of logs, and we expect it to do anyhing BUT break the system and cause unavailability. Whether it be an error message (too many logs), a better handling of the logs (i.e. in chunks) or a better memory management, all is acceptable. For a script like this to crash a server is unacceptable in an enterprise environmemt.\n\n4. How would the customer like to achieve this? (List the functional requirements here)\n\nCustomer is expecting better memory Management in logconv.pl in below ways.\n- refusing to start processing logs altogether when logconv.pl calculates the logs are too big to be processed in memory\n- processing logs in sizeable chunks and later adding these processed chunks together to do a final report\n- fine-tune the memory usage of logconv.pl\n- finding temporary diskspace to flush parts of memory (of course with the option of still one of the previous three when disk space is too low)\n\n5. For each functional requirement listed in question 4, specify how Red Hat and the customer can test to confirm the requirement is successfully implemented.\nCreate a replica setup which generate 5 GB of daily logs & try to run logconv.pl.\n\n6. Is there already an existing RFE upstream or in Red Hat bugzilla?\nNo\n\n7. How quickly does this need resolved? (desired target release)\nNo time-line\n\n8. Does this request meet the RHEL Bug and Feature Inclusion Criteria (please review)\nYes\n\n9. List the affected packages\n389-ds-base\n\n10. Would the customer be able to assist in testing this functionality if implemented?\nYes\n\n--- Additional comment from Rich Megginson on 2012-07-31 13:49:14 EDT ---\n\nUpstream ticket:\nhttps://fedorahosted.org/389/ticket/419\n\n--- Additional comment from Rich Megginson on 2012-08-06 16:32:03 EDT ---\n\nCan you provide the exact command line being used?\n\n--- Additional comment from Arpit Tolani on 2012-08-06 17:12:02 EDT ---\n\n(In reply to comment #2)\n> Can you provide the exact command line being used?\n\n/usr/local/bin/logconv.pl -efcibaltnxrgjyp /var/log/dirsrv/slapd-$INST/access.`TZ=CST+24 date +%Y%m%d`* > $REPORT 2> /dev/null\n\nAfter communicating that -alicbf are very expensive, trying without these doesn't seem to crash the servers & they are happy with workaround. They want to use all options to get a full report in the future.\n\n--- Additional comment from Rich Megginson on 2012-08-06 17:23:55 EDT ---\n\n(In reply to comment #3)\n> (In reply to comment #2)\n> > Can you provide the exact command line being used?\n> \n> /usr/local/bin/logconv.pl -efcibaltnxrgjyp\n> /var/log/dirsrv/slapd-$INST/access.`TZ=CST+24 date +%Y%m%d`* > $REPORT 2>\n> /dev/null\n> \n> After communicating that -alicbf are very expensive, trying without these\n> doesn't seem to crash the servers & they are happy with workaround. The script uses hashes, and uses the string value(search base, search filter, bind dn, etc)) as the key.  There's just a ton of keys when processing so many logs, and the memory usage will be very high.\n\nOne option would be to do what I suggested above and build that logic into the tool, but this means it will take a lot longer to run(separate parsings of the logs for each option).\n\n--- Additional comment from RHEL Product and Program Management on 2012-12-13 14:46:47 EST ---\n\nSince this bug report was entered in bugzilla, the release flag has been\nset to ? to ensure that it is properly evaluated for this release.\n\n--- Additional comment from  on 2013-01-15 15:41:50 EST ---\n\nThis is the new logconv.pl (v7.0) that will be included in 389 1.3.1\n\n--- Additional comment from  on 2013-01-15 15:44:15 EST ---\n\nHere are some generic test stats to show the new memory improvement:\n\n Logconv.pl 6.1 (old version):\n\n    1 million lines:  2843256 k\n    5 million lines:  5118708 k\n\n Logconv.pl 7.0 (new version):\n\n    1 million lines:  2026828 k\n    5 million lines:  2029848 k\n\n--- Additional comment from Rich Megginson on 2013-10-01 19:26:42 EDT ---\n\nmoving all ON_QA bugs to MODIFIED in order to add them to the errata (can't add bugs in the ON_QA state to an errata).           "text": "Description of problem:\n\nTroubleshooting host issues through the vdsm.log file is difficult. Easily parsing usable information for quick diagnostics of key data is not possible today. RHEV hypervisors need to have a simple and dedicate local log file that contains a set of self-diagnostic information about the network status that can assist in easily identifying common infrastructure issues. \n\nProposed solution:\n\nOn each host, the following network data should be logged on a regular user-definable interval which defaults to 60 seconds:\n\n- Physical NICs and Bonds link status (up/down) \n\n- ICMP pings to the hosts' default gateways. Each interval should run a certain number of ICMP requests, which is user-definable. The default value should be 10 requests\n\n\nAdditional info:\n\nThe new dedicated log file should be -\n\n- In simple format that is easily consumable by end users, support staff, and engineers. The format should make it simple to use CLI parsing such as grep or awk to find and list key information\n\n- Stored on each hypervisor host\n\n- Included in SOS Report Bundles\n\n- Available for view/display within the RHEV-Manager UI when the host is online",

          "text": "1. Proposed title of this feature request  \n  Container Memory Limit Option\n  \n2. Who is the customer behind the request?  \nAccount: name DREAMWORKS ANIMATION 313249 \nTAM customer: yes  \nSRM customer: yes  \nStrategic: yes  \n  \n3. What is the nature and description of the request?  \n\nAs an application, it is beneficial to know what your memory limit is, so that it dynamic memory allocation settings can be set for containers of different sizes. \n  \n4. Why does the customer need this? (List the business requirements here)  \n\nSome software applications find it useful to use this information to correctly preallocate memory for internal caches, etc. and it would be great to know if there's a standard interface to get at it from within your container.\n  \n5. How would the customer like to achieve this? (List the functional requirements here)  \n\nCurrent work around is to use: \n\n[root@localhost ~]# MEM_VAL=512k; docker run -i -t -m $MEM_VAL -e MEM_VAL=$MEM_VAL --rm rhel7 /bin/bash\nbash-4.2# echo $MEM_VAL\n512k\n\nHowever this is not a solution that work if the container is allow to alter is memory settings live. \n  \n6. In fact,  winbind has a similar functionality here for what the customer is requesting, so the RFE would bring closer\nfeature parity-wise to winbind.\n\n4. Why does the customer need this? (''ldap\ngroup'' would be ''ldap^group'').
